# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Plugin Backend Query to Data Frame Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Grafana datasource plugin query flows from the HTTP API handler to a data frame response. Find Go source files in grafana/grafana implementing: the query API handler, the plugin client call, the backend query execution, and the data frame serialization.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

59-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Grafana datasource plugin query flow and created a comprehensive answer. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Query Flow Chain

The complete flow from HTTP API handler to data frame response:

1. **HTTP API Handler** (`pkg/api/ds_query.go` - `QueryMetricsV2`)
   - Entry point at `/api/ds/query` endpoint
   - Parses incoming request and delegates to query service

2. **Query Data Service** (`pkg/services/query/query.go`)
   - Routes queries to appropriate handlers
   - For single datasource: `handleQuerySingleDatasource()` calls `pluginClient.QueryData()`

3. **Plugin Client** (`pkg/plugins/plugins.go` - `QueryData`)
   - Wrapper that gets the backend plugin client
   - Delegates to gRPC plugin client

4. **Backend Plugin gRPC Client** (`pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go` - `QueryData`)
   - Actual gRPC communication with backend plugin
   - Returns `backend.QueryDataResponse` with data frames

5. **Aggregator Plugin Handler** (`pkg/aggregator/apiserver/plugin/query.go` - `QueryDataHandler`)
   - Alternative path for aggregator-based plugins
   - Decodes JSON request, calls plugin client, wraps response

6. **Response Serialization** (`pkg/aggregator/apiserver/util/responder.go` - `Object`)
   - Uses `responsewriters.WriteRawJSON()` to serialize response
   - Kubernetes API server handles JSON encoding

7. **Response Structure** (`pkg/aggregator/apis/aggregation/v0alpha1/types.go` - `QueryDataResponse`)
   - Wraps `backend.QueryDataResponse` 
   - Contains data frames with query results

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, symbols, execution chain, and detailed narrative.

Query Data Service\\n**File**: `pkg/services/query/query.go`\\n**Functions**: `queryData()`, `handleQuerySingleDatasource()` (lines 101-331)\\n\\nThe `queryData()` method:\\n- Parses the metric request into queries grouped by datasource\\n- Routes to appropriate handler: expressions, single datasource, or concurrent queries\\n- For single datasource queries, calls `handleQuerySingleDatasource()` which:\\n  - Gets the datasource and validates access\\n  - Checks if query-service is available via `qsDatasourceClientBuilder.BuildClient()`\\n  - For single-tenant flow: calls `s.pluginClient.QueryData()` directly at line 322\\n  - For multi-tenant flow: converts to k8s request and calls query-service client\\n\\n### 3. Plugin Client Query Execution\\n**File**: `pkg/plugins/plugins.go`\\n**Function**: `QueryData()` (lines 329-335)\\n\\nThe Plugin struct's `QueryData()` method:\\n- Gets the plugin client via `p.Client()`\\n- Delegates to the actual backend plugin client (usually gRPC-based)\\n\\n### 4. Backend Plugin gRPC Client\\n**File**: `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go`\\n**Function**: `QueryData()` (lines 162-166)\\n\\nThe ClientV2's `QueryData()` method:\\n- Checks if `DataClient` is available\\n- Calls the gRPC service to execute the query on the backend plugin\\n- Returns `*backend.QueryDataResponse` containing the query results and data frames\\n\\n### 5. Alternative: Aggregator Plugin Handler\\n**File**: `pkg/aggregator/apiserver/plugin/query.go`\\n**Function**: `QueryDataHandler()` (lines 20-89)\\n\\nFor aggregator-based plugins:\\n- Receives HTTP request containing `data.QueryDataRequest`\\n- Decodes JSON into `data.QueryDataRequest` (line 26)\\n- Converts to backend.QueryDataRequest format (line 75)\\n- Calls `h.client.QueryData()` (the plugin client)\\n- Wraps response in `aggregationv0alpha1.QueryDataResponse`\\n\\n### 6. HTTP Response Serialization\\n**File**: `pkg/aggregator/apiserver/util/responder.go`\\n**Function**: `Object()` (lines 16-18)\\n\\nThe `Responder.Object()` method:\\n- Takes the status code and response object\\n- Calls `responsewriters.WriteRawJSON()` from Kubernetes API server library\\n- This uses the runtime.Object encoding to serialize the response to JSON\\n\\n### 7. Response Data Structure\\n**File**: `pkg/aggregator/apis/aggregation/v0alpha1/types.go`\\n**Struct**: `QueryDataResponse` (lines 130-136)\\n\\nThe `QueryDataResponse` struct:\\n- Embeds Kubernetes TypeMeta (for API versioning)\\n- Wraps `backend.QueryDataResponse` from grafana-plugin-sdk-go\\n- The `backend.QueryDataResponse` contains a map of `RefID -> DataResponse`\\n- Each `DataResponse` contains:\\n  - `Frames: []*data.Frame` - Array of data frames containing the query results\\n  - `Error` - Optional error message\\n  - Status information\\n\\n### Data Frame Serialization\\nData frames are serialized as part of the `backend.QueryDataResponse` JSON encoding. The frames contain:\\n- Field definitions (name, type, labels)\\n- Field values (time series data, logs, etc.)\\n- Frame metadata (type, ref ID, etc.)\\n\\nThis complete flow ensures that:\\n1. Frontend queries reach the HTTP API\\n2. Queries are routed to appropriate datasource plugins\\n3. Backend plugins execute and return results as data frames\\n4. Results are serialized to JSON and returned to the frontend\\n\"",
